## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). The equation of motion generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator with nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and/or periodic forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (damped, driven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Cubic + quadratic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (periodic external driving)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v**3 (position-dependent or cubic damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Combined Duffing-Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (mixed nonlinearities)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic restoring with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation; even powers (x²) break symmetry — look for symmetric vs asymmetric behavior in data
- Position-dependent damping terms like x²*v indicate Van der Pol-type self-excitation where damping changes sign depending on amplitude
- Explicit time dependence typically appears as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicating periodic external driving forces
- If acceleration depends only on x (not v or t), the system is conservative and energy is preserved — check if v-dependence is significant
- Cubic restoring force x³ with same/opposite sign as linear term x indicates hardening/softening spring behavior respectively
- Velocity-odd terms (v, v³) represent dissipation; velocity-even terms (v², v*|v|) represent direction-dependent forces like aerodynamic drag
- Products of position and time functions (x*cos(c*t)) suggest parametric excitation rather than direct forcing
- Phase-space symmetry: if dv_dt is odd in both x and v simultaneously, the system has time-reversal symmetry properties
